A future to believe in!

One could forgive practically every voter in the country, yourself included, for being shocked. Two years ago, pollsters hardly included you in the race. When you declared your candidacy, most articles made sure to highlight that you were a long shot. Why wouldn’t they? You were going up against Hillary Clinton. And yet, you said it best in a quote added as an addendum to most of those articles at the bottom of the page:

‘I think people should be a little bit careful underestimating me'

Now, you have managed, despite it all, despite the primaries, despite running as a third party candidate in a country where one hasn’t won a state since the sixties, to outright win more than 270 votes in the electoral college. And not just that: you won comfortably when near-every outlet predicted a contingent election, at best.

No, believe it one cannot. Your opponents hardly offer a concession the day of, likely unable to believe their eyes; they’re joined by your wife, Jane, by your supporters, awestruck to what can only be described as a political revolution.

The Republican Party has already declared its response to your victory: the newly debuted Fox host, Tucker Carlson, declares that an undemocratic communist revolution has taken hold of the United States. ‘The Bolsheviks have just stormed the Winter Palace,’ he declares , ‘and we cannot stand by.’ The Democratic Party, meanwhile, has reacted with pure confusion. Some certainly want to work with you: after all, the most left-wing President of the United States has just won: what else is there to do? Others, chiefly Hillary, have behind the scenes pushed something else (from what you’ve heard,) and she’s joined by other influential voices.

  

If you would like, you certainly have an opening to stage a takeover of the Democratic Party, perhaps starting next year with the DNC chairmanship, but be warned: this is a party that his been incredibly hostile to you, and many of those likely to support you have been pushed out. Several leftists have managed to join Congress, a few even winning outside of the two parties, such as Gayle McLaughlin of the Greens. It is only a handful though: not enough to exert control, although shockingly, Democrats have managed to take both Houses of Congress, likely thanks to Trump backed third parties. It may not be enough to pass Medicare For All, but that's for you to negotiate.

Regardless, you will be America’s first socialist President, come January. You will at least have four years, and re-election might be in the cards, but who knows in what form? There will likely be an attempt to change the electoral system of this country after what happened this year, but you will likely have a role in that as well. The world watches as you start packing for Washington.

If you listen, you can hear a whisper.

Plenty of things can happen before that, so buckle up: it’s going to be a long few weeks.
